<rating>1<//rating>< review>
First let me say this we had Stanley Steamer out to clean our carpets and they did a terrible job, we have been using them for at least 20 years for rentals and our house and this time they didn't even clean the carpet.  Our carpet is two years old and we have just gotten a new puppy that we had to potty train so there were several pet stains, we were clear with green carpet what was up with our carpet and the Stanley steamer angle.  They of course told us Stanley steamer was the worst and I had to agree.

The day of the cleaning Donovan shows up in an unmarked personal van with the steam cleaner, he cleaned our carpet and did a much better job than Stanley Steamer did and charged us $350 for 3 rooms, kinda pricey but ok.  Donovan told us no problem he would make us happy with the carpet, when the carpet dried  several spots came back, as clean as the carpet was we felt that maybe these just didn't get hit with the pre treatment,  This is where the problems start, we contacted back the company to get this taken care of, they became un helpful and asked for $150 dollars more to come back out.  I was like what happened to making us happy?  When I said I was not going to pay an additional $150 for the carpet to get touched up Green carpet essentially stopped replying to my text's.  Of course they have cashed the check by then.

I wanted to give them a good review but when I started dealing with them after the fact I became suspicious of the way they are running this business, I believe they are just contracting the work out so you have no way of getting them back and when you look at there page there clearly is no satisfaction guarantee, and they don't follow the procedure that they layout as what they do.  I also noticed that some of the reviews seem to be questionable and are posted by the same names that sent out my receipt.

Buyer beware, I can not recommend you to do business with this company because I don't think they care if your carpet cleaning is to your satisfaction.  I imagine they will post a reply to this negative review but oh well seems there are others that have had this experience.

(edit)

Within 5 mins of posting this review I received this text from  Paida Ndemera the person I have been in contact with trying to work this out.

"Hi. Thank you for the review. I‚Äôll assume there is no longer mileage in trying to rectify this issue"

she has not responded to my text since this text and hadn't responded for 3 days to the previous texts, never had a company refuse to work something out because you posted a negative review.  Just another reason to not use these guys in my opinion.
Art<//review>

< Text>
The cost and estimate:  I called for a quote to see if the service was something that was in my price range.  I talked to the guy and he quoted around $200 for the job. It was for around 500sf of carpet cleaning.  He mentioned that price was for the lowest service, but when the guy arrives I should ask him and he might give me a deal for the more expensive service.  He said "maybe $270". I agreed.  When the guy arrives he's telling me around $400. I said that was way above my limit so he came down to, I believe, $320.  He promised me it would be great, he uses all natural cleansers, and I would love the service and results. At that time I mentioned that I didn't like I didn't like that the cost was so much higher but the fact was, I wanted my carpets cleaned and the guy was there and ready to do the job. I just went with it.

The results: Cut to the carpets are now cleaned.  Do they look better, yes. Are they what I expected, no. I fully realize the carpets where dirty and definitely not ever going to be perfect  but the result I got was nothing better than what I get when I rent the Rug Dr at Safeway for $30. I told him I was moderately pleased and he had a lot of reasons why he couldn't get it to a better standard but all I saw was $320 wasted.  I have cleaned my carpets with the rented machine multiple times (and was very happy for the $30 I spent) so I guess I expected the results from a professional services to be so much better.  That weren't.

To top it off when he leaving I asked how I should pay, he said "Vemno"  and that I "could tip there if I wanted".  I didn't know that tipping was a thing that you did for a professional service like this but I did anyway.

Bottom line:  I spent $350 for a service that did no better than I have done myself for $30 using a rented carpet cleaner from the grocery store.

Maybe my expectations were too high but I will never use this service again.  Just not what I expected.< /Text>

<Date>1477806300882</Date><Rating>4<//Rating>< text>
I had a couple bottles to recycle and had so much fun at my last recycling experience in Seven Trees that I wanted to try it again!  It had been so much time since my last adventure that I forgot what a complete waste of time this actually is.  For me, at least, however if you dedicate your time to picking up this stuff and have more than a few bottles, this might be worth it.  But even then I'm not really sure.  The time it takes to get out here and wait in various lines vs the convenience of just putting it out on the curb... well you can decide for yourself.

This place has different lines for the different kinds of material, but there are no instructions.  i'm sure the other patrons were laughing at the white girl doing recycling wrong.

For those thinking that I had a bad experience, you are sorely wrong.  I enjoyed finally getting it right, the employees that I talked to were all very friendly, and the wait was much shorter than my experience at the Seven Trees place.  I can't comment on the dollar value as I really don't care about the difference in a few cents for my few bottles.  Also - this place is outdoor.  You will appreciate that after having to wait in a long line in an un-airconditioned warehouse with a bunch of trash.< /text>

<name>Cathy Aguilar< /name><Date>1383116970919<//Date><rating>5</rating>< text>
From the moment I pull my car into the driveway at Ranchtown recycling until the time when I'm ready to head back onto Lincoln Ave. to go on with my day, there is always someone right there ready to help.  The funny thing is, they always make me feel like I'm the only one they are there to help.  One of the "guys" directs me to the next parking place and by the time I'm unlocking the back, someone else is heading my way asking if I need any bins for bottles. They bring the tubs, we fill 'em up, and then together we make one long pull over to the scale.  Sure I can do it on my own, but it's faster to have help and adds a little conversation to my day. I have been taking our family's recycling there for 15 + years and I can't remember ever running into someone with a bad attitude.  They have always answered my questions and have helped me locate anything I need.  A+ service, organization and attitude. Thanks for lots of smiles (and cash).<//text>

< text>
I dealt with Joe and Rick (hope I got your name right!).

Firstly, this was my first experience getting maintenance done in the bay area. So I was ready for some sticker shock. I had rear pads and rotors + oil change.

I was advised very well about what needed to be done, and what was recommended. I requested a few extra services be skipped and Dorso's obliged without complaint. So the sales approach is low pressure and friendly.

My only complaint was that I wasn't offered anything other than OEM or preferred parts. "Back home" many shops will offer cheaper (new) parts with your approval and if you waive a warranty on the service. I was NOT offered this and as a result the total was very pricey.

Lastly, I was entirely pleased with the professionalism. All removed parts were kept and shown to me. Everyone was very friendly. No one got upset when I refused additional services. And future service recommendations (and where to get them) were provided.

Dorso's seems like a great first stop for your auto service. In the future I might comparison price shop a bit before plunking down a ton of money for something I used to be able to do in my own driveway for 1/10th the cost. But perhaps that's just the way things are in the Bay Area... And since I can't service my own cars anymore, maybe I need to adjust my expectations.</text>

<rate>5< /rate><Text>This is my favorite japanese style crepe place. I have been coming here for years and it never disappoints. First time was in 2011.

Toppings and ingredients are always fresh. The creeper batter is always amazing, lots of flavor and the right amount of chewiness to lightness.

Prices can get high if you build your own crepe, but the location is in Beverly Hills..

I always get the Nutty Banana with earl grey crepe but they no longer have the earl grey. A little disappointing but they have other great choices.

Staff is friendly, and the place is quite small. So, if you catch it at a busy time, it's tough to move around.</Text><pics>None< /pics>< response>

< date>
1408426381098</date>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< Text>
I had a Harajuku Crepe in Japan and this place in Beverly Hills tasted better!! :) I'm impressed! :D

This is a cute little cafe in Beverly Hills. There are about 2 small tables and a couch for seating. The guy who makes the crepes is Japanese and is really nice!

If you're here, you gotta try a crepe. You can also order boba or tea too. How it works is that you get to customize your crepe by which type of crepe you want, fruits, toppings, fillings, and/or ice cream. And with each thing you choose, there's a cost.

What I got:
-Earl grey crepe $3
-Strawberries $1
-Whipped cream $0.50
-Nutella $0.50
-Green tea ice cream $0.50

Total: $6 (Totally worth it!!)

The crepe was thin and perfectly cooked! Everything was well-portioned and wasn't too sweet.

Only downside is the parking. You gotta try to find a meter or park in one of the public lots/garages.

Overall, I am a fan and will definitely be back! A great place for dessert!<//Text>

This place is located in the  heart of Beverly Hills,  right off of rodeo drive.  It's kind of a hole in the wall,  which is weird because of its location.

This place is so damn good!

<Text>Don't really understand what the hype is around Harajuku Crepes. Came here on a Saturday 15 minutes before closing and was amazed by how affordable these crepes are, and the option of choosing sesame and earl grey crepe batter. But after asking the cashier, I decided to stick with the original batter, since it was most popular. Included in the crepe, I had banana, sheet of mochi, nutella, and almonds (they ran out of whipped cream). The crepe itself was $3, and the toppings ranged form $0.25 - $1. Mine came out to be $6-7.

When I received my crepe, I noticed how small it was and how little toppings it came with... No wonder why it was so cheap! Secondly, just from holding the crepe, I already knew it wouldn't be good (or as good as other crepes I've had), because it wasn't the crispy crepe. It was really soft, like a pancake, which I'm not really a fan of.

It wasn't a "bad" crepe per se, but just not my cup of tea. I probably wouldn't come back...<//Text></record></dataset><record>
<user>116183414117229479123< /user><Name>Paulina Lei<//Name><date>1497983804115</date>< Rating>
3</Rating>
< Text>
I came here with a group of 9 on a Friday night. I got a matcha crepe with vanilla ice cream, whipped cream, and mochi. It came out to be $6. The crepe was rather smaller than other places, but still pretty good. The mochi was wrapped within the edges of the crepe, allowing me to eat ice cream and mochi in every bite.

One downside is that the place is rather small, so there wasn't much seating and we ended up standing outside to eat the crepes. In addition, waiting for the crepes took a while, especially considering the size of the crepes and the lack of customers while we were there.

Parking is also hard to find. Had to park near a park a block away.

Overall, not a bad crepe place, but definitely have had better with faster service.

Note: There is a minimum credit card charge of $6.</Text>

<Text>Harajuku Crepe is a fantastic place to take a break from all the Rodeo Drive window shopping ;) Crepes here are A-MA-ZING!

The owner developed his skills at a creperie in Japan, and invented his own recipe for this venture. The not-so-secret ingredient that makes the crepes here extra special is MOCHI powder! It makes the crepe itself slightly thicker than French style crepes while still maintaining the fluffy softness we looove.

What's also great is the selection of flavors--original, green tea, earl grey and buckwheat (yes, buckwheat!)--ensures that you're never going to get bored of the menu. Since they're very generous with their toppings, the finished crepes are often monstrous.

Finally, a worthy successor to the now defunct crepe nazi on Sawtelle!< /Text>< Pics>
